# Repository Guidelines

## Project Structure & Module Organization

This repository is the Zed editor monorepo with Oxidian knowledge-base crates under `crates/`: `oxidian_core`, `oxidian_vault`, `oxidian_backlinks`, `oxidian_daily`, and `oxidian_frontmatter`. The dependency flow is `oxidian_core` -> `oxidian_vault` -> feature crates. Main Rust packages live in `crates/`, extensions in `extensions/`, tooling in `tooling/`, scripts in `script/`, and mdBook documentation in `docs/`. Oxidian workspace entries are marked in the root `Cargo.toml` with `# OXIDIAN BEGIN` / `# OXIDIAN END`.

## Build, Test, and Development Commands

- `cargo build -p zed`: build the main editor target.
- `cargo build --workspace`: build every workspace package.
- `cargo nextest run -p <crate> --no-fail-fast`: run tests for one crate.
- `cargo nextest run --workspace --no-fail-fast`: run the full test suite.
- `./script/clippy`: run the repository lint pipeline; use this instead of `cargo clippy`.
- `cargo fmt --all`: format Rust code with edition/style edition 2024.
- `./script/prettier`: format JavaScript and documentation assets.
- `cargo xtask workflows`: regenerate generated GitHub workflow files.

## Coding Style & Naming Conventions

Use Rust 2024 conventions and repository formatting. Do not introduce `mod.rs`; prefer `src/<name>.rs` and explicit `[lib] path = "...rs"` entries where needed. Avoid `unwrap()` in production code, propagate errors with `?`, and do not discard fallible results with `let _ =`; log or handle them explicitly. `clippy.toml` denies `std::process::Command`, `smol::Timer::after`, and `serde_json::from_reader`.

## Testing Guidelines

Tests run through `cargo nextest`. Database-sensitive tests should use the existing `sequential-db-tests` nextest group. Some collaboration tests require Postgres. For GPUI async tests, prefer `cx.background_executor().timer(duration).await` over `smol::Timer::after(...)` so `run_until_parked()` can track scheduled work reliably.

## Commit & Pull Request Guidelines

Use imperative PR titles without conventional-commit prefixes, for example `oxidian_vault: Fix wiki-link indexing`. Keep titles concise and avoid trailing punctuation. PR bodies should explain behavior changes, list relevant tests, link issues when applicable, and end with:

```markdown
Release Notes:

- Fixed ...
```

Use `- N/A` when there is no user-facing change.

## Agent-Specific Instructions

Keep Oxidian changes scoped to the five `oxidian_*` crates unless integration work requires touching Zed packages. Preserve generated files unless the documented regeneration command was run.

```

Reference these files when providing feedback:\n\n- [Chapter 1 - Coding Styles and Idioms](references/chapter_01.md): Borrowing vs cloning, Copy trait, Option/Result handling, iterators, comments\n- [Chapter 2 - Clippy and Linting](references/chapter_02.md): Clippy configuration, important lints, workspace lint setup\n- [Chapter 3 - Performance Mindset](references/chapter_03.md): Profiling, avoiding redundant clones, stack vs heap, zero-cost abstractions\n- [Chapter 4 - Error Handling](references/chapter_04.md): Result vs panic, thiserror vs anyhow, error hierarchies\n- [Chapter 5 - Automated Testing](references/chapter_05.md): Test naming, one assertion per test, snapshot testing\n- [Chapter 6 - Generics and Dispatch](references/chapter_06.md): Static vs dynamic dispatch, trait objects\n- [Chapter 7 - Type State Pattern](references/chapter_07.md): Compile-time state safety, when to use it\n- [Chapter 8 - Comments vs Documentation](references/chapter_08.md): When to comment, doc comments, rustdoc\n- [Chapter 9 - Understanding Pointers](references/chapter_09.md): Thread safety, Send/Sync, pointer types\n\n## Quick Reference\n\n### Borrowing & Ownership\n- Prefer `&T` over `.clone()` unless ownership transfer is required\n- Use `&str` over `String`, `&[T]` over `Vec<T>` in function parameters\n- Small `Copy` types (≤24 bytes) can be passed by value\n- Use `Cow<'_, T>` when ownership is ambiguous\n\n### Error Handling\n- Return `Result<T, E>` for fallible operations; avoid `panic!` in production\n- Never use `unwrap()`/`expect()` outside tests\n- Use `thiserror` for library errors, `anyhow` for binaries only\n- Prefer `?` operator over match chains for error propagation\n\n### Performance\n- Always benchmark with `--release` flag\n- Run `cargo clippy -- -D clippy::perf` for performance hints\n- Avoid cloning in loops; use `.iter()` instead of `.into_iter()` for Copy types\n- Prefer iterators over manual loops; avoid intermediate `.collect()` calls\n\n### Linting\nRun regularly: `cargo clippy --all-targets --all-features --locked -- -D warnings`\n\nKey lints to watch:\n- `redundant_clone` - unnecessary cloning\n- `large_enum_variant` - oversized variants (consider boxing)\n- `needless_collect` - premature collection\n\nUse `#[expect(clippy::lint)]` over `#[allow(...)]` with justification comment.\n\n### Testing\n- Name tests descriptively: `process_should_return_error_when_input_empty()`\n- One assertion per test when possible\n- Use doc tests (`///`) for public API examples\n- Consider `cargo insta` for snapshot testing generated output\n\n### Generics & Dispatch\n- Prefer generics (static dispatch) for performance-critical code\n- Use `dyn Trait` only when heterogeneous collections are needed\n- Box at API boundaries, not internally\n\n### Type State Pattern\nEncode valid states in the type system to catch invalid operations at compile time:\n```rust\nstruct Connection<State> { /* ... */ _state: PhantomData<State> }\nstruct Disconnected;\nstruct Connected;\n\nimpl Connection<Connected> {\n    fn send(&self, data: &[u8]) { /* only connected can send */ }\n}\n```\n\n### Documentation\n- `//` comments explain *why* (safety, workarounds, design rationale)\n- `///` doc comments explain *what* and *how* for public APIs\n- Every `TODO` needs a linked issue: `// TODO(#42): ...`\n- Enable `#![deny(missing_docs)]` for libraries\n",

  "source": "unified_exec_startup",
  "stdout": "# Chapter 4 - Errors Handling\n\nRust enforces a strict error handling approach, but *how* you handle them defines where your code feels ergonomic, consistent and safe - as opposing cryptic and painful. This chapter dives into best practices for modeling and managing fallible operations across libraries and binaries.\n\n> Even if you decide to crash you application with `unwrap` or `expect`, Rust forces you to declare that intentionally.\n\n## 4.1 Prefer `Result`, avoid panic 🫨\n\nRust has a powerful type that wraps fallible data, [`Result<T, E>`](https://doc.rust-lang.org/std/result/), this allows us to handle Error cases according to our needs and manage the state of the application based on that.\n\n* If your function can fail, prefer to return a `Result`:\n```rust\nfn divide(x: f64, y: f64) -> Result<f64, DivisionError> {\n    if y == 0.0 {\n        Err(DivisionError::DividedByZero)\n    } else {\n        Ok(x / y)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n* Use `panic!` only in unrecoverable conditions - typically tests, assertions, bugs or a need to crash the application for some explicit reason.\n* There are 3 relevant macros that can replace `panic!` in appropriate conditions:\n    * `todo!`, similar to panic, but alerts the compiler that you are aware that there is code missing.\n    * `unreachable!`, you have reasoned about the code block and are sure that condition `xyz` is not possible and if ever becomes possible you want to be alerted.\n    * `unimplemented!`, specially useful for alerting that a block is not yet implement with a reason.\n\n## 4.2 Avoid `unwrap`/`expect` in Production\n\nAlthough `expect` is preferred to `unwrap`, as it can have context, they should be avoided in production code as there are smarter alternatives to them. Considering that, they should be used in the following scenarios:\n- In tests, assertions or test helper functions.\n- When failure is impossible.\n- When the smarter options can't handle the specific case.\n\n### 🚨 Alternative ways of handling `unwrap`/`expect`:\n\n* If your `Result` (or `Option`) can have a predefined early return value in case of `Result::Err`, that doesn't need to know the `Err` value, use `let Ok(..) = else { return ... }` pattern, as it helps with flatten functions:\n```rust\nlet Ok(json) = serde_json::from_str(&input) else {\n    return Err(MyError::InvalidJson);\n}\n```\n* If your `Result` (or `Option`) needs error recovery in case of `Result::Err`, that doesn't need to know the `Err` value, use `if let Ok(..) else { ... }` pattern:\n```rust\nif let Ok(json) = serde_json::from_str(&input) else {\n    ...\n} else {\n    Err(do_something_with_input(&input))\n}\n```\n* Functions that can have to handle `Option::None` values are recommended to return `Result<T, E>`, where `E` is a crate or module level error, like the examples above.\n* Lastly `unwrap_or`, `unwrap_or_else` or `unwrap_or_default`, these functions help you create alternative exits to unwrap that manage the uninitialized values.\n\n## 4.3 `thiserror` for Crate level errors\n\nDeriving Error manually is verbose and error prone, the rust ecosystem has a really good crate to help with this, `thiserror`. It allows you to create error types that easily implement `From` trait as well as easy error message (`Display`), improving developer experience while working seamlessly with `?` and integrating with `std::error::Error`:\n\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)]\npub enum MyError {\n    #[error(\"Network Timeout\")]\n    Timeout,\n    #[error(\"Invalid data: {0}\")]\n    InvalidData(String),\n    #[error(transparent)]\n    Serialization(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n    #[error(\"Invalid request information. Header: {headers}, Metadata: {metadata}\")]\n    InvalidRequest {\n        headers: Headers,\n        metadata: Metadata\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Error Hierarchies and Wrapping\n\nFor layered systems the best practice is to use nested `enum/struct` errors with `#[from]`:\n\n```rust\nuse crate::database::DbError;\nuse crate::external_services::ExternalHttpError;\n\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)]\npub enum ServiceError {\n    #[error(\"Database handler error: {0}\")]\n    Db(#[from] DbError),\n    #[error(\"External services error: {0}\")]\n    ExternalServices(#[from] ExternalHttpError)\n}\n```\n\n## 4.4 Reserve `anyhow` for Binaries\n\n`anyhow` is an amazing crate, and quite useful for projects that are beginning and need accelerated speed. However, there is a turning point where it just painfully propagates through your code, considering this, `anyhow` is recommended only for **binaries**, where ergonomic error handling is needed and there is no need for precise error types:\n\n```rust\nuse anyhow::{Context, Result, anyhow};\n\nfn main() -> Result<()> {\n    let content = std::fs::read_to_string(\"config.json\")\n        .context(\"Failed to read config file\")?;\n    Config::from_str(&content)\n        .map_err(|err| anyhow!(\"Config parsing error: {err}\"))\n}\n```\n\n### 🚨 `Anyhow` Gotchas\n\n* Keeping the `context` and `anyhow` strings up-to-date in all code base is harder than keeping `thiserror` messages as you don't have a single point of entry.\n* `anyhow::Result` erases context that a caller might need, so avoid using it in a library.\n* test helper functions can use `anyhow` with little to no issues.\n\n## 4.5 Use `?` to Bubble Errors\n\nPrefer using `?` over verbose alternatives like `match` chains:\n```rust\nfn handle_request(req: &Request) -> Result<ValidatedRequest, MyError> {\n    validate_headers(req)?;\n    validate_body_format(req)?;\n    validate_credentials(req)?;\n    let body = Body::try_from(req)?;\n\n    Ok(ValidatedRequest::try_from((req, body))?)\n}\n```\n\n> In case error recovery is needed, use `or_else`, `map_err`, `if let Ok(..) else`. To **inspect or log your error**, use `inspect_err`.\n\n## 4.6 Unit Test should exercise errors\n\nWhile many errors don't implement PartialEq and Eq, making it hard to do direct assertions between them, it is possible to check the error messages with `format!` or `to_string()`, making the errors meaningful and test validated:\n\n```rust\n#[test]\nfn error_does_not_implement_partial_eq() {\n    let err = divide(10., 0.0).unwrap_err();\n    assert_eq!(err.to_string(), \"division by zero\");\n}\n\n#[test]\nfn error_implements_partial_eq() {\n    let err = process(my_value).unwrap_err();\n\n    assert_eq!(\n        err,\n        MyError {\n            ..\n        }\n    )\n}\n```\n\n## 4.7 Important Topics\n\n### Custom Error Structs\n\nSometimes you don't need an enum to handle your errors, as there is only one type of error that your module can have. This can be solved with `struct Errors`:\n\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error, PartialEq)]\n#[error(\"Request failed with code `{code}`: {message}\")]\nstruct HttpError {\n    code: u16,\n    message: String\n}\n```\n\n### Async Errors\n\nWhen using async runtimes, like Tokio, make sure that your errors implement `Send + Sync + 'static` where needed, specially in tasks or across `.await` boundaries:\n\n```rust\n#[tokio::main]\nasync fn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error + Send + Sync>> {\n    ...\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n> Avoid `Box<dyn std::error::Error>` in libraries unless it is really needed\n",
  "stderr": "",

However, there is a turning point where it just painfully propagates through your code, considering this, `anyhow` is recommended only for **binaries**, where ergonomic error handling is needed and there is no need for precise error types:\n\n```rust\nuse anyhow::{Context, Result, anyhow};\n\nfn main() -> Result<()> {\n    let content = std::fs::read_to_string(\"config.json\")\n        .context(\"Failed to read config file\")?;\n    Config::from_str(&content)\n        .map_err(|err| anyhow!(\"Config parsing error: {err}\"))\n}\n```\n\n### 🚨 `Anyhow` Gotchas\n\n* Keeping the `context` and `anyhow` strings up-to-date in all code base is harder than keeping `thiserror` messages as you don't have a single point of entry.\n* `anyhow::Result` erases context that a caller might need, so avoid using it in a library.\n* test helper functions can use `anyhow` with little to no issues.\n\n## 4.5 Use `?` to Bubble Errors\n\nPrefer using `?` over verbose alternatives like `match` chains:\n```rust\nfn handle_request(req: &Request) -> Result<ValidatedRequest, MyError> {\n    validate_headers(req)?;\n    validate_body_format(req)?;\n    validate_credentials(req)?;\n    let body = Body::try_from(req)?;\n\n    Ok(ValidatedRequest::try_from((req, body))?)\n}\n```\n\n> In case error recovery is needed, use `or_else`, `map_err`, `if let Ok(..) else`. To **inspect or log your error**, use `inspect_err`.\n\n## 4.6 Unit Test should exercise errors\n\nWhile many errors don't implement PartialEq and Eq, making it hard to do direct assertions between them, it is possible to check the error messages with `format!` or `to_string()`, making the errors meaningful and test validated:\n\n```rust\n#[test]\nfn error_does_not_implement_partial_eq() {\n    let err = divide(10., 0.0).unwrap_err();\n    assert_eq!(err.to_string(), \"division by zero\");\n}\n\n#[test]\nfn error_implements_partial_eq() {\n    let err = process(my_value).unwrap_err();\n\n    assert_eq!(\n        err,\n        MyError {\n            ..\n        }\n    )\n}\n```\n\n## 4.7 Important Topics\n\n### Custom Error Structs\n\nSometimes you don't need an enum to handle your errors, as there is only one type of error that your module can have. This can be solved with `struct Errors`:\n\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error, PartialEq)]\n#[error(\"Request failed with code `{code}`: {message}\")]\nstruct HttpError {\n    code: u16,\n    message: String\n}\n```\n\n### Async Errors\n\nWhen using async runtimes, like Tokio, make sure that your errors implement `Send + Sync + 'static` where needed, specially in tasks or across `.await` boundaries:\n\n```rust\n#[tokio::main]\nasync fn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error + Send + Sync>> {\n    ...\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n> Avoid `Box<dyn std::error::Error>` in libraries unless it is really needed\n",
  "exit_code": 0,
  "duration": {
    "secs": 0,
    "nanos": 10508
  },
  "formatted_output": "# Chapter 4 - Errors Handling\n\nRust enforces a strict error handling approach, but *how* you handle them defines where your code feels ergonomic, consistent and safe - as opposing cryptic and painful. This chapter dives into best practices for modeling and managing fallible operations across libraries and binaries.\n\n> Even if you decide to crash you application with `unwrap` or `expect`, Rust forces you to declare that intentionally.\n\n## 4.1 Prefer `Result`, avoid panic 🫨\n\nRust has a powerful type that wraps fallible data, [`Result<T, E>`](https://doc.rust-lang.org/std/result/), this allows us to handle Error cases according to our needs and manage the state of the application based on that.\n\n* If your function can fail, prefer to return a `Result`:\n```rust\nfn divide(x: f64, y: f64) -> Result<f64, DivisionError> {\n    if y == 0.0 {\n        Err(DivisionError::DividedByZero)\n    } else {\n        Ok(x / y)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n* Use `panic!` only in unrecoverable conditions - typically tests, assertions, bugs or a need to crash the application for some explicit reason.\n* There are 3 relevant macros that can replace `panic!` in appropriate conditions:\n    * `todo!`, similar to panic, but alerts the compiler that you are aware that there is code missing.\n    * `unreachable!`, you have reasoned about the code block and are sure that condition `xyz` is not possible and if ever becomes possible you want to be alerted.\n    * `unimplemented!`, specially useful for alerting that a block is not yet implement with a reason.\n\n## 4.2 Avoid `unwrap`/`expect` in Production\n\nAlthough `expect` is preferred to `unwrap`, as it can have context, they should be avoided in production code as there are smarter alternatives to them. Considering that, they should be used in the following scenarios:\n- In tests, assertions or test helper functions.\n- When failure is impossible.\n- When the smarter options can't handle the specific case.\n\n### 🚨 Alternative ways of handling `unwrap`/`expect`:\n\n* If your `Result` (or `Option`) can have a predefined early return value in case of `Result::Err`, that doesn't need to know the `Err` value, use `let Ok(..) = else { return ... }` pattern, as it helps with flatten functions:\n```rust\nlet Ok(json) = serde_json::from_str(&input) else {\n    return Err(MyError::InvalidJson);\n}\n```\n* If your `Result` (or `Option`) needs error recovery in case of `Result::Err`, that doesn't need to know the `Err` value, use `if let Ok(..) else { ... }` pattern:\n```rust\nif let Ok(json) = serde_json::from_str(&input) else {\n    ...\n} else {\n    Err(do_something_with_input(&input))\n}\n```\n* Functions that can have to handle `Option::None` values are recommended to return `Result<T, E>`, where `E` is a crate or module level error, like the examples above.\n* Lastly `unwrap_or`, `unwrap_or_else` or `unwrap_or_default`, these functions help you create alternative exits to unwrap that manage the uninitialized values.\n\n## 4.3 `thiserror` for Crate level errors\n\nDeriving Error manually is verbose and error prone, the rust ecosystem has a really good crate to help with this, `thiserror`. It allows you to create error types that easily implement `From` trait as well as easy error message (`Display`), improving developer experience while working seamlessly with `?` and integrating with `std::error::Error`:\n\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)]\npub enum MyError {\n    #[error(\"Network Timeout\")]\n    Timeout,\n    #[error(\"Invalid data: {0}\")]\n    InvalidData(String),\n    #[error(transparent)]\n    Serialization(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n    #[error(\"Invalid request information. Header: {headers}, Metadata: {metadata}\")]\n    InvalidRequest {\n        headers: Headers,\n        metadata: Metadata\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Error Hierarchies and Wrapping\n\nFor layered systems the best practice is to use nested `enum/struct` errors with `#[from]`:\n\n```rust\nuse crate::database::DbError;\nuse crate::external_services::ExternalHttpError;\n\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)]\npub enum ServiceError {\n    #[error(\"Database handler error: {0}\")]\n    Db(#[from] DbError),\n    #[error(\"External services error: {0}\")]\n    ExternalServices(#[from] ExternalHttpError)\n}\n```\n\n## 4.4 Reserve `anyhow` for Binaries\n\n`anyhow` is an amazing crate, and quite useful for projects that are beginning and need accelerated speed. However, there is a turning point where it just painfully propagates through your code, considering this, `anyhow` is recommended only for **binaries**, where ergonomic error handling is needed and there is no need for precise error types:\n\n```rust\nuse anyhow::{Context, Result, anyhow};\n\nfn main() -> Result<()> {\n    let content = std::fs::read_to_string(\"config.json\")\n        .context(\"Failed to read config file\")?;\n    Config::from_str(&content)\n        .map_err(|err| anyhow!(\"Config parsing error: {err}\"))\n}\n```\n\n### 🚨 `Anyhow` Gotchas\n\n* Keeping the `context` and `anyhow` strings up-to-date in all code base is harder than keeping `thiserror` messages as you don't have a single point of entry.\n* `anyhow::Result` erases context that a caller might need, so avoid using it in a library.\n* test helper functions can use `anyhow` with little to no issues.\n\n## 4.5 Use `?` to Bubble Errors\n\nPrefer using `?` over verbose alternatives like `match` chains:\n```rust\nfn handle_request(req: &Request) -> Result<ValidatedRequest, MyError> {\n    validate_headers(req)?;\n    validate_body_format(req)?;\n    validate_credentials(req)?;\n    let body = Body::try_from(req)?;\n\n    Ok(ValidatedRequest::try_from((req, body))?)\n}\n```\n\n> In case error recovery is needed, use `or_else`, `map_err`, `if let Ok(..) else`. To **inspect or log your error**, use `inspect_err`.\n\n## 4.6 Unit Test should exercise errors\n\nWhile many errors don't implement PartialEq and Eq, making it hard to do direct assertions between them, it is possible to check the error messages with `format!` or `to_string()`, making the errors meaningful and test validated:\n\n```rust\n#[test]\nfn error_does_not_implement_partial_eq() {\n    let err = divide(10., 0.0).unwrap_err();\n    assert_eq!(err.to_string(), \"division by zero\");\n}\n\n#[test]\nfn error_implements_partial_eq() {\n    let err = process(my_value).unwrap_err();\n\n    assert_eq!(\n        err,\n        MyError {\n            ..\n        }\n    )\n}\n```\n\n## 4.7 Important Topics\n\n### Custom Error Structs\n\nSometimes you don't need an enum to handle your errors, as there is only one type of error that your module can have. This can be solved with `struct Errors`:\n\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error, PartialEq)]\n#[error(\"Request failed with code `{code}`: {message}\")]\nstruct HttpError {\n    code: u16,\n    message: String\n}\n```\n\n### Async Errors\n\nWhen using async runtimes, like Tokio, make sure that your errors implement `Send + Sync + 'static` where needed, specially in tasks or across `.await` boundaries:\n\n```rust\n#[tokio::main]\nasync fn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error + Send + Sync>> {\n    ...\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n> Avoid `Box<dyn std::error::Error>` in libraries unless it is really needed\n",

  "stdout": "# Chapter 1 - Coding Styles and Idioms\n\n## 1.1 Borrowing Over Cloning\n\nRust's ownership system encourages **borrow** (`&T`) instead of **cloning** (`T.clone()`). \n> ❗ Performance recommendation\n\n### ✅ When to `Clone`:\n\n* You need to change the object AND preserve the original object (immutable snapshots).\n* When you have `Arc` or `Rc` pointers.\n* When data is shared across threads, usually `Arc`.\n* Avoid massive refactoring of non performance critical code.\n* When caching results (dummy example below):\n```rust\nfn get_config(&self) -> Config {\n    self.cached_config.clone()\n}\n```\n* When the underlying API expects Owned Data.\n\n### 🚨 `Clone` traps to avoid:\n\n* Auto-cloning inside loops `.map(|x| x.clone)`, prefer to call `.cloned()` or `.copied()` at the end of the iterator.\n* Cloning large data structures like `Vec<T>` or `HashMap<K, V>`.\n* Clone because of bad API design instead of adjusting lifetimes.\n* Prefer `&[T]` instead of `Vec<T>` or `&Vec<T>`.\n* Prefer `&str` or `&String` instead of `String`.\n* Prefer `&T` instead of `T`.\n* Clone a reference argument, if you need ownership, make it explicit in the arguments for the caller. Example:\n```rust\nfn take_a_borrow(thing: &Thing) {\n    let thing_cloned = thing.clone(); // the caller should have passed ownership instead\n}\n```\n\n### ✅ Prefer borrowing:\n```rust\nfn process(name: &str) {\n    println!(\"Hello {name}\");\n}\n\nlet user = String::from(\"foo\");\nprocess(&user);\n```\n\n### ❌ Avoid redundant cloning:\n```rust\nfn process_string(name: String) {\n    println!(\"Hello {name}\");\n}\n\nlet user = String::from(\"foo\");\nprocess(user.clone()); // Unnecessary clone\n```\n\n## 1.2 When to pass by value? (Copy trait)\n\nNot all types should be passed by reference (`&T`). If a type is **small** and it is **cheap to copy**, it is often better to **pass it by value**. Rust makes it explicit via the `Copy` trait.\n\n### ✅ When to pass by value, `Copy`:\n* The type **implements** `Copy` (`u32`, `bool`, `f32`, small structs).\n* The cost of moving the value is negligible.\n\n```rust\nfn increment(x: u32) -> u32 {\n    x + 1\n}\n\nlet num = 1;\nlet new_num = increment(num); // `num` still usable after this point\n```\n\n### ❓ Which structs should be `Copy`?\n* When to consider declaring `Copy` on your own types:\n* All fields are `Copy` themselves.\n* The struct is `small`, up to 2 (maybe 3) words of memory or 24 bytes (each word is 64 bits/8bytes).\n* The struct **represents a \"plain data object\"**, without resourcing to ownership (no heap allocations. Example: `Vec` and `Strings`).\n\n❗**Rust Arrays are stack allocated.** Which means they can be copied if their underlying type is `Copy`, but this will be allocated in the program stack which can easily become a stack overflow. More on [Chapter 3 - Stack vs Heap](./chapter_03.md#33-stack-vs-heap-be-size-smart)\n\nFor reference, each primitive type size in bytes:\n\n#### Integers:\n\n| Type | Size |\n|------------- |---------- |\n| i8 u8 | 1 byte |\n| i16 u16 | 2 bytes |\n| i32 u32 | 4 bytes |\n| i64 u64 | 8 bytes |\n| isize usize | Arch |\n| i128 u128 | 16 bytes |\n\n#### Floating Point:\n\n| Type | Size |\n|---------- |---------- |\n| f32 | 4 bytes |\n| f64 | 8 bytes |\n\n\n#### Other:\n\n| Type | Size |\n|---------- |---------- |\n| bool | 1 byte |\n| char | 4 bytes |\n\n\n### ✅ Good struct to derive `Copy`:\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone)]\nstruct Point {\n    x: f32,\n    y: f32,\n    z: f32\n}\n```\n\n### ❌ Bad struct to derive `Copy`:\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\nstruct BadIdea {\n    age: i32,\n    name: String, // String is not `Copy`\n}\n```\n\n### ❓Which Enums should be `Copy`?\n* If your enum acts like tags and atoms.\n* The enum payloads are all `Copy`.\n* **❗Enums size are based on their largest element.**\n\n### ✅ Good Enum to derive\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone)]\nenum Direction {\n    North,\n    South,\n    East,\n    West,\n}\n```\n\n## 1.3 Handling `Option<T>` and `Result<T, E>`\nRust 1.65 introduced a better way to safely unpack Option and Result types with the `let Some(x) = … else { … }` or `let Ok(x) = … else { … }` when you have a default `return` value, `continue` or `break` default else case. It allows early returns when the missing case is **expected and normal**, not exceptional.\n\n### ✅ Cases to use each pattern matching for Option and Return\n* Use `match` when you want to pattern match against the inner types `T` and `E`\n```rust\nmatch self {\n    Ok(Direction::South) => { … },\n    Ok(Direction::North) => { … },\n    Ok(Direction::East) => { … },\n    Ok(Direction::West) => { … },\n    Err(E::One) => { … },\n    Err(E::Two) => { … },\n}\n\nmatch self {\n    Some(3|5) => { … }\n    Some(x) if x > 10 => { … }\n    Some(x) => { … }\n    None => { … }\n}\n```\n\n* Use `match` when your type is transformed into something more complex Like `Result<T, E>` becoming `Result<Option<T>, E>`.\n```rust\nmatch self {\n    Ok(t) => Ok(Some(t)),\n    Err(E::Empty) => Ok(None),\n    Err(err) => Err(err),\n}\n```\n\n* Use `let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }` when the divergent code doesn't need to know about the failed pattern matches or doesn't need extra computation:\n```rust\nlet Some(&Direction::North) = self.direction.as_ref() else {\n    return Err(DirectionNotAvailable(self.direction));\n}\n```\n\n* Use `let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }` when you want to break or continue a pattern match\n```rust\nfor x in self {\n    let Some(x) = x else {\n        continue;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n* Use `if let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }` when `DIVERGING_CODE` needs extra computation:\n```rust\nif let Some(x) = self.next() {\n    // computation\n} else {\n    // computation when `None/Err` or not matched\n}\n```\n\n❗**If you don't care about the value of the `Err` case, please use `?` to propagate the `Err` to the caller.**\n\n### ❌ Bad Option/Return pattern matching:\n\n* Conversion between Result and Option (prefer `.ok()`,`.ok_or()`, and `ok_or_else()`)\n```rust\nmatch self {\n    Ok(t) => Some(t),\n    Err(_) => None\n}\n```\n\n* `if let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }` when divergent code is a default or pre-computed value (prefer `let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }`):\n```rust\nif let Some(values) = self.next() {\n    // computation\n    (Some(..), values)\n} else {\n",

  "formatted_output": "# Chapter 1 - Coding Styles and Idioms\n\n## 1.1 Borrowing Over Cloning\n\nRust's ownership system encourages **borrow** (`&T`) instead of **cloning** (`T.clone()`). \n> ❗ Performance recommendation\n\n### ✅ When to `Clone`:\n\n* You need to change the object AND preserve the original object (immutable snapshots).\n* When you have `Arc` or `Rc` pointers.\n* When data is shared across threads, usually `Arc`.\n* Avoid massive refactoring of non performance critical code.\n* When caching results (dummy example below):\n```rust\nfn get_config(&self) -> Config {\n    self.cached_config.clone()\n}\n```\n* When the underlying API expects Owned Data.\n\n### 🚨 `Clone` traps to avoid:\n\n* Auto-cloning inside loops `.map(|x| x.clone)`, prefer to call `.cloned()` or `.copied()` at the end of the iterator.\n* Cloning large data structures like `Vec<T>` or `HashMap<K, V>`.\n* Clone because of bad API design instead of adjusting lifetimes.\n* Prefer `&[T]` instead of `Vec<T>` or `&Vec<T>`.\n* Prefer `&str` or `&String` instead of `String`.\n* Prefer `&T` instead of `T`.\n* Clone a reference argument, if you need ownership, make it explicit in the arguments for the caller. Example:\n```rust\nfn take_a_borrow(thing: &Thing) {\n    let thing_cloned = thing.clone(); // the caller should have passed ownership instead\n}\n```\n\n### ✅ Prefer borrowing:\n```rust\nfn process(name: &str) {\n    println!(\"Hello {name}\");\n}\n\nlet user = String::from(\"foo\");\nprocess(&user);\n```\n\n### ❌ Avoid redundant cloning:\n```rust\nfn process_string(name: String) {\n    println!(\"Hello {name}\");\n}\n\nlet user = String::from(\"foo\");\nprocess(user.clone()); // Unnecessary clone\n```\n\n## 1.2 When to pass by value? (Copy trait)\n\nNot all types should be passed by reference (`&T`). If a type is **small** and it is **cheap to copy**, it is often better to **pass it by value**. Rust makes it explicit via the `Copy` trait.\n\n### ✅ When to pass by value, `Copy`:\n* The type **implements** `Copy` (`u32`, `bool`, `f32`, small structs).\n* The cost of moving the value is negligible.\n\n```rust\nfn increment(x: u32) -> u32 {\n    x + 1\n}\n\nlet num = 1;\nlet new_num = increment(num); // `num` still usable after this point\n```\n\n### ❓ Which structs should be `Copy`?\n* When to consider declaring `Copy` on your own types:\n* All fields are `Copy` themselves.\n* The struct is `small`, up to 2 (maybe 3) words of memory or 24 bytes (each word is 64 bits/8bytes).\n* The struct **represents a \"plain data object\"**, without resourcing to ownership (no heap allocations. Example: `Vec` and `Strings`).\n\n❗**Rust Arrays are stack allocated.** Which means they can be copied if their underlying type is `Copy`, but this will be allocated in the program stack which can easily become a stack overflow. More on [Chapter 3 - Stack vs Heap](./chapter_03.md#33-stack-vs-heap-be-size-smart)\n\nFor reference, each primitive type size in bytes:\n\n#### Integers:\n\n| Type | Size |\n|------------- |---------- |\n| i8 u8 | 1 byte |\n| i16 u16 | 2 bytes |\n| i32 u32 | 4 bytes |\n| i64 u64 | 8 bytes |\n| isize usize | Arch |\n| i128 u128 | 16 bytes |\n\n#### Floating Point:\n\n| Type | Size |\n|---------- |---------- |\n| f32 | 4 bytes |\n| f64 | 8 bytes |\n\n\n#### Other:\n\n| Type | Size |\n|---------- |---------- |\n| bool | 1 byte |\n| char | 4 bytes |\n\n\n### ✅ Good struct to derive `Copy`:\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone)]\nstruct Point {\n    x: f32,\n    y: f32,\n    z: f32\n}\n```\n\n### ❌ Bad struct to derive `Copy`:\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\nstruct BadIdea {\n    age: i32,\n    name: String, // String is not `Copy`\n}\n```\n\n### ❓Which Enums should be `Copy`?\n* If your enum acts like tags and atoms.\n* The enum payloads are all `Copy`.\n* **❗Enums size are based on their largest element.**\n\n### ✅ Good Enum to derive\n```rust\n#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone)]\nenum Direction {\n    North,\n    South,\n    East,\n    West,\n}\n```\n\n## 1.3 Handling `Option<T>` and `Result<T, E>`\nRust 1.65 introduced a better way to safely unpack Option and Result types with the `let Some(x) = … else { … }` or `let Ok(x) = … else { … }` when you have a default `return` value, `continue` or `break` default else case. It allows early returns when the missing case is **expected and normal**, not exceptional.\n\n### ✅ Cases to use each pattern matching for Option and Return\n* Use `match` when you want to pattern match against the inner types `T` and `E`\n```rust\nmatch self {\n    Ok(Direction::South) => { … },\n    Ok(Direction::North) => { … },\n    Ok(Direction::East) => { … },\n    Ok(Direction::West) => { … },\n    Err(E::One) => { … },\n    Err(E::Two) => { … },\n}\n\nmatch self {\n    Some(3|5) => { … }\n    Some(x) if x > 10 => { … }\n    Some(x) => { … }\n    None => { … }\n}\n```\n\n* Use `match` when your type is transformed into something more complex Like `Result<T, E>` becoming `Result<Option<T>, E>`.\n```rust\nmatch self {\n    Ok(t) => Ok(Some(t)),\n    Err(E::Empty) => Ok(None),\n    Err(err) => Err(err),\n}\n```\n\n* Use `let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }` when the divergent code doesn't need to know about the failed pattern matches or doesn't need extra computation:\n```rust\nlet Some(&Direction::North) = self.direction.as_ref() else {\n    return Err(DirectionNotAvailable(self.direction));\n}\n```\n\n* Use `let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }` when you want to break or continue a pattern match\n```rust\nfor x in self {\n    let Some(x) = x else {\n        continue;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n* Use `if let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }` when `DIVERGING_CODE` needs extra computation:\n```rust\nif let Some(x) = self.next() {\n    // computation\n} else {\n    // computation when `None/Err` or not matched\n}\n```\n\n❗**If you don't care about the value of the `Err` case, please use `?` to propagate the `Err` to the caller.**\n\n### ❌ Bad Option/Return pattern matching:\n\n* Conversion between Result and Option (prefer `.ok()`,`.ok_or()`, and `ok_or_else()`)\n```rust\nmatch self {\n    Ok(t) => Some(t),\n    Err(_) => None\n}\n```\n\n* `if let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }` when divergent code is a default or pre-computed value (prefer `let PATTERN = EXPRESSION else { DIVERGING_CODE; }`):\n```rust\nif let Some(values) = self.next() {\n    // computation\n    (Some(..), values)\n} else {\n",
  "status": "completed"
}

  "stdout": "# Chapter 5 - Automated Testing\n\n> Tests are not just for correctness. They are the first place people look to understand how your code works.\n\n* Tests in rust are declared with the attribute macro `#[test]`. Most code editors can compile and run the functions declared under the macro individually or blocks of them.\n* Test can have special compilation flags with `#[cfg(test)]`. Also executable in code editors if it contained `#[test]`, it is a good way to mock complicated functions or override traits.\n\n## 5.1 Tests as Living Documentation\n\nIn Rust, as in many other languages, tests often show how the functions are meant to be used. If a test is clear and targeted, it's often more helpful than reading the function body, when combined with other tests, they serve as living documentation.\n\n### Use descriptive names\n\n> In the unit test name we should see the following:\n> * `unit_of_work`: which *function* we are calling. The **action** that will be executed. This is often be the name of the the test `mod` where the function is being tested.\n```rust\n#[cfg(test)] \nmod test { \n    mod function_name { \n        #[test] \n        fn returns_y_when_x() { ... } \n    } \n}\n```\n> * `expected_behavior`: the set of **assertions** that we need to verify that the test works.\n> * `state_that_the_test_will_check`: the general **arrangement**, or setup, of the specific test case.\n\n#### ❌ Don't use a generic name for a test\n```rust\n#[test]\nfn test_add_happy_path() {\n    assert_eq!(add(2, 2), 4);\n}\n```\n#### ✅ Use a name which reads like a sentence, describing the desired behavior\n> Alternatively, if you function has too many tests, you can blob them together in a `mod`, it makes it easier to read and navigate.\n\n```rust\n// OPTION 1\n#[test]\nfn process_should_return_blob_when_larger_than_b() {\n    let a = setup_a_to_be_xyz();\n    let b = Some(2);\n    let expected = MyExpectedStruct { ... };\n\n    let result = process(a, b).unwrap();\n\n    assert_eq!(result, expected);\n}\n\n// OPTION 2\nmod process {\n    #[test]\n    fn should_return_blob_when_larger_than_b() {\n        let a = setup_a_to_be_xyz();\n        let b = Some(2);\n        let expected = MyExpectedStruct { ... };\n\n        let result = process(a, b).unwrap();\n\n        assert_eq!(result, expected);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n> When executing `cargo test` the test output for each option will look like:\n> Option 1: `process_should_return_blob_when_larger_than_b`.\n> Option 2: `process::should_return_blob_when_larger_than_b`.\n\n### Use modules for organization\n\nMost IDEs can run a single module of tests all together.\nThe test name in the output will also contain the name of the module.\nTogether, that means you can use the module name to group related tests together:\n\n```rust\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod test { // IDEs will provide a ▶️ button here\n\n    mod process {\n        #[test] // IDEs will provide a ▶️ button here\n        fn returns_error_xyz_when_b_is_negative() {\n            let a = setup_a_to_be_xyz();\n            let b = Some(-5);\n            let expected = MyError::Xyz;\n            \n            let result = process(a, b).unwrap_err();\n            \n            assert_eq!(result, expected);\n        }\n\n        #[test] // IDEs will provide a ▶️ button here\n        fn returns_invalid_input_error_when_a_and_b_not_present() {\n            let a = None;\n            let b = None;\n            let expected = MyError::InvalidInput;\n\n            let result = process(a, b).unwrap_err();\n\n            assert_eq!(result, expected);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Only test one behavior per function\n\nTo keep tests clear, they should describe _one_ thing that the unit does.\nThis makes it easier to understand why a test is failing.\n\n#### ❌ Don't test multiple things in the same test\n```rust\nfn test_thing_parser(...) {\n    assert!(Thing::parse(\"abcd\").is_ok());\n    assert!(Thing::parse(\"ABCD\").is_err());\n}\n```\n\n#### ✅ Test one thing per test\n```rust\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod test_thing_parser {\n    #[test]\n    fn lowercase_letters_are_valid() {\n        assert!(\n            Thing::parse(\"abcd\").is_ok(),\n            // Works like `eprintln`, `format` and `println` macros\n            \"Thing parse error: {:?}\", \n            Thing::parse(\"abcd\").unwrap_err()\n        );\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn capital_letters_are_invalid() {\n        assert!(Thing::parse(\"ABCD\").is_err());\n    }\n}\n```\n\n> `Ok` scenarios should have an `eprintln` of the `Err` case.\n\n### Use very few, ideally one, assertion per test\n\nWhen there are multiple assertions per test, it's both harder to understand the intended behavior and \noften requires many iterations to fix a broken test, as you work through assertions one by one.\n\n❌ Don't include many assertions in one test:\n\n```rust\n#[test]\nfn test_valid_inputs() {\n    assert!(the_function(\"a\").is_ok());\n    assert!(the_function(\"ab\").is_ok());\n    assert!(the_function(\"ba\").is_ok());\n    assert!(the_function(\"bab\").is_ok());\n}\n```\n\nIf you are testing separate behaviors, make multiple tests each with descriptive names.\nTo avoid boilerplate, either use a shared setup function or [rstest](https://crates.io/crates/rstest) cases *with descriptive test names*:\n```rust\n#[rstest]\n#[case::single(\"a\")]\n#[case::first_letter(\"ab\")]\n#[case::last_letter(\"ba\")]\n#[case::in_the_middle(\"bab\")]\nfn the_function_accepts_all_strings_with_a(#[case] input: &str) {\n    assert!(the_function(input).is_ok());\n}\n```\n\n> Considerations when using `rstest`\n>\n> * It's harder for both IDEs and humans to run/locate specific tests.\n> * Expectation vs condition naming is now visually inverted (expectation first).\n\n## 5.2 Add Test Examples to your Docs\n\nWe will deep dive into docs at a later stage, so in this section we will just briefly go over how to add tests to you docs. Rustdoc can turn examples into executable tests using `///` with a few advantages:\n\n",

names*:\n```rust\n#[rstest]\n#[case::single(\"a\")]\n#[case::first_letter(\"ab\")]\n#[case::last_letter(\"ba\")]\n#[case::in_the_middle(\"bab\")]\nfn the_function_accepts_all_strings_with_a(#[case] input: &str) {\n    assert!(the_function(input).is_ok());\n}\n```\n\n> Considerations when using `rstest`\n>\n> * It's harder for both IDEs and humans to run/locate specific tests.\n> * Expectation vs condition naming is now visually inverted (expectation first).\n\n## 5.2 Add Test Examples to your Docs\n\nWe will deep dive into docs at a later stage, so in this section we will just briefly go over how to add tests to you docs. Rustdoc can turn examples into executable tests using `///` with a few advantages:\n\n",
  "status": "completed"
}

pub heading: Option<Arc<str>>,\n}\n\nimpl WikiLink {\n    /// Parses the inner content of a wiki-link (without the surrounding `[[` and `]]`).\n    pub fn parse(inner: &str) -> Self {\n        let (target_and_heading, alias) = if let Some(pipe_pos) = inner.find('|') {\n            let alias = inner[pipe_pos + 1..].trim();\n            (&inner[..pipe_pos], Some(Arc::from(alias)))\n        } else line.\n/// If yes, returns the inner content of the wiki-link.\npub fn find_wiki_link_at_column(line: &str, col: usize) -> Option<String> {\n    let chars: Vec<char> = line.chars().collect();\n    \n    // Look backwards from col for \"[[\"\n    let mut open_idx = None;\n    if col >= 2 {\n        for i in (0..=col.min(chars.len() - 2)).rev() {\n            if chars[i] == '[' && chars[i+1] == '[' {\n                open_idx = Some(i + 2);\n                break;\n            }\n            if chars[i] == ']' && chars[i+1] == ']' && i + 2 <= col {\n                return None;\n            }\n 2 <= chars.len() && chars[i] == ']' && chars[i+1] == ']' {\n            close_idx = Some(i);\n            break;\n        }\n        if i + 2 <= chars.len() && chars[i] == '[' && chars[i+1] == '[' {\n            return None;\n        }\n    }\n\n    let Some(end) = close_idx else { return None; };\n\n    if col >= start - 2 && col <= end + 2 {\n        let content: String = chars[start..end].iter().collect();\n        Some(content)\n    } else {\n        None\n    }\n}\n\n/// A thread-safe global resolver for wiki-links.\n/// Registered by `oxidian_vault` and called by    &self.0\n    }\n}\n\nimpl std::fmt::Display for NoteId {\n    fn fmt(&self, formatter: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {\n        formatter.write_str(&self.0)\n    }\n}\n\n/// A parsed `[[wiki-link]]`, including optional alias and heading anchor.\n///\n/// Examples:\n/// - `[[My Note]]`              → target=\"My Note\", alias=None, heading=None\n/// - `[[My Note|Display Name]]` → target=\"My Note\", alias=Some(\"Display Name\"), heading=None\n/// - `[[My Note#Section]]`      → target=\"My Note\", alias=None, heading=Some(\"Section\")\n/// - `[[My Note#Section|Name]]` → target=\"My Note\", alias=Some(\"Name\"), heading=Some(\"Section\")\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub struct WikiLink {\n    pub target: Arc<str>,\n    pub alias: Option<Arc<str>>,\n    pub heading: Option<Arc<str>>,\n}\n\nimpl WikiLink {\n    /// Parses the inner content of a wiki-link (without the surrounding `[[` and `]]`).\n    pub fn parse(inner: &str) -> Self {\n        let (target_and_heading, alias) = if let Some(pipe_pos) = inner.find('|') {\n            let alias = inner[pipe_pos + 1..].trim();\n            (&inner[..pipe_pos], Some(Arc::from(alias)))\n        } else {\n            (inner, None)\n        };\n\n        let (target, heading) = if let Some(hash_pos) = target_and_heading.find('#') {\n            let heading = target_and_heading[hash_pos + 1..].trim();\n            (&target_and_heading[..hash_pos], Some(Arc::from(heading)))\n        } else {\n            (target_and_heading, None)\n        };\n\n        Self {\n            target: Arc::from(target.trim()),\n            alias,\n            heading,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the display text for this link: the alias if present, otherwise the target.\n    pub fn display_text(&self) -> &str {\n        if let Some(alias) = &self.alias {\n            alias\n        } else {\n            &self.target\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Vault-level configuration, stored in `.oxidian/config.json` at the vault root.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug)]\npub struct VaultConfig {\n    /// Absolute path to the vault root directory.\n    pub root: PathBuf,\n    /// Path to the templates directory, relative to vault root.\n    pub templates_dir: PathBuf,\n    /// Path where daily notes are stored, relative to vault root.\n    pub daily_notes_dir: PathBuf,\n    /// Date format string for daily notes filenames (e.g. `\"YYYY-MM-DD\"`).\n    pub daily_notes_format: Arc<str>,\n    /// Separator character used between target and alias in wiki-links (default: `|`).\n    pub wiki_link_alias_separator: char,\n    /// Optional path to the Marksman binary for LSP integration.\n    pub marksman_binary: Option<PathBuf>,\n    /// Whether telemetry and Zed cloud features are line.\n/// If yes, returns the inner content of the wiki-link.\npub fn find_wiki_link_at_column(line: &str, col: usize) -> Option<String> {\n    let chars: Vec<char> = line.chars().collect();\n    \n    // Look backwards from col for \"[[\"\n    let mut open_idx = None;\n    if col >= 2 {\n        for i in (0..=col.min(chars.len() - 2)).rev() {\n            if chars[i] == '[' && chars[i+1] == '[' {\n                open_idx = Some(i + 2);\n                break;\n            }\n            if chars[i] == ']' && chars[i+1] == ']' && i + 2 <= col {\n                return None;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    let Some(start) = open_idx else { return None; };\n\n    // Look forwards from start for \"]]\"\n    let mut close_idx = None;\n    for i in start..chars.len() {\n        if i + 2 <= chars.len() && chars[i] == ']' && chars[i+1] == ']' {\n            close_idx = Some(i);\n            break;\n        }\n        if i + 2 <= chars.len() && chars[i] == '[' && chars[i+1] == '[' {\n            return None;\n        }\n    }\n\n    let Some(end) = close_idx else { return None; };\n\n    if col >= start - 2 && col <= end + 2 {\n        let content: String = chars[start..end].iter().collect();\n        Some(content)\n    } else {\n        None\n    }\n}\n\n/// A thread-safe global resolver for wiki-links.\n/// Registered by `oxidian_vault` and called by `editor` to navigate to notes.\npub struct WikiLinkResolver(\n    pub Arc<dyn Fn(&str, &mut gpui::Window, &mut gpui::App) -> Option<PathBuf> + Send + Sync>,\n);\n\nimpl gpui::Global for WikiLinkResolver {}\n\n// OXIDIAN BEGIN\npub struct MarksmanBinaryPath(pub Option<PathBuf>);\nimpl gpui::Global for MarksmanBinaryPath {}\n// OXIDIAN END\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use the UI layer.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub enum VaultEvent {\n    /// A note was added or re-indexed.\n    NoteIndexed(NoteId),\n    /// A note was removed from the vault.\n    NoteRemoved(NoteId),\n    /// The full vault scan completed.\n    InitialScanComplete,\n}\n\n/// The vault index: watches the vault directory and keeps the SQLite index up to date.\npub struct VaultIndex {\n    pub config: VaultConfig,\n    db: VaultDatabase,\n    /// All currently known note IDs, mapped to their absolute paths.\n    notes: HashMap<NoteId, PathBuf>,\n    _watcher_task: Task<()>,\n}\n\nimpl EventEmitter<VaultEvent> for VaultIndex {}\n\nimpl VaultIndex {\n    /// Creates and starts a new vault index for the given config.\n    /// Immediately starts a background scan of the vault directory.\n    pub fn new(\n        config: VaultConfig,\n        fs: Arc<dyn Fs>,\n        cx: &mut Context<Self>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let db = VaultDatabase::global(cx);\n\n        let vault_root = config.root.clone();\n        let (scan_sender, scan_receiver) = channel::unbounded::<PathBuf>();\n\n        let watcher_task = cx.spawn({\n            let fs = fs.clone();\n            async move |this, cx| {\n                // Initial scan — enumerate all .md files in the vault\n                if let Ok(entries) = Self::scan_vault_directory(&vault_root, &*fs).await {\n                    for path in entries {\n                        scan_sender.send(path).await.ok();\n                    }\n                }\n\n                while let Ok(path) = scan_receiver.recv().await {\n                    let note_id = Self::note_id_for_path(&vault_root, &path);\n                    let Some(note_id) = note_id else { continue };\n\n                    if let Err(err) = this.update(cx, |vault, cx| {\n                        vault.index_note(note_id.clone(), path, cx)\n                    }) {\n                        log::error!(\"VaultIndex: entity gone while indexing {note_id}: {err}\");\n                        break;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        });\n\n        Self {\n            config,\n            db,\n            notes: HashMap::default(),\n            _watcher_task: watcher_task,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the absolute path for a given `NoteId`, if it's in the index.\n    pub fn resolve_note(&self, note_id: &NoteId) -> Option<&PathBuf> {\n        self.notes.get(note_id)\n    }\n\n    /// Fuzzy-resolves a wiki-link target string to the best matching `NoteId`.\n    /// Tries exact match first, then basename match, then prefix match.\n    pub fn resolve_wiki_link(&self, target: &str) -> Option<NoteId> {\n        let normalized = target.trim();\n\n        // Exact match\n        let candidate = NoteId::from_relative_path(normalized);\n        if self.notes.contains_key(&candidate) {\n            return Some(candidate);\n        }\n\n        // Basename match (target matches the last component of the path)\n        for note_id in self.notes.keys() {\n            let basename = note_id\n                .as_str()\n                .rsplit('/')\n                .next()\n                .unwrap_or(note_id.as_str());\n            if basename.eq_ignore_ascii_case(normalized) {\n                return Some(note_id.clone());\n            }\n        }\n\n        None\n    }\n\n    /// close_rel;\n                let inner = &line[after_open..close_abs];\n\n                // Skip empty links and links containing newlines (shouldn't happen in single line)\n                if Result<Vec<PathBuf>> {\n        let root = root.to_path_buf();\n        // Run the directory scan on the thread pool since std::fs is synchronous\n        smol::unblock(move || {\n            let mut markdown_files = Vec::new();\n            let mut stack = vec![root];\n\n            while let Some(dir) = stack.pop() {\n                let entries = std::fs::read_dir(&dir)\n                    .context(\"scanning vault directory\")?;\n\n                for entry in entries {\n                    let entry = entry.context(\"reading directory entry\")?;\n                    let path = entry.path();\n                    let file_name = entry.file_name();\n                    let name = file_name.to_string_lossy();\n\n                    // Skip hidden directories (including .oxidian, .git, etc.)\n                    if name.starts_with('.') {\n                        continue;\n                    }\n\n                    let metadata = entry.metadata().context(\"reading entry metadata\")?;\n\n                    if metadata.is_dir() {\n                        stack.push(path);\n                    } else if path.extension().is_some_and(|ext| ext == \"md\") {\n                        markdown_files.push(path);\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n\n            Ok(markdown_files)\n        })\n        .await\n    }\n\n    fn (line_number, WikiLink) pairs.\n/// This runs before pulldown-cmark to capture `[[...]]` syntax.\npub fn extract_wiki_links_from_text(text: &str) -> Vec<(usize, WikiLink)> {\n    let mut results = Vec::new();\n\n    for (line_index, line) in text.lines().enumerate() {\n        let mut search_start = 0;\n\n        while let Some(open) = line[search_start..].find(\"[[\") {\n            let open_abs = search_start + open;\n            let after_open = open_abs + 2;\n\n            if let Some(close_rel) = line[after_open..].find(\"]]\") {\n                let close_abs = after_open + close_rel;\n                let inner = &line[after_open..close_abs];\n\n                // Skip empty links and links containing newlines (shouldn't happen in single line)\n                if !inner.is_empty() {\n                    results.push((line_index + 1, WikiLink::parse(inner)));\n                }\n\n                search_start = close_abs + 2;\n            } else {\n                // No closing ]] on this line — skip rest of line\n                break;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    results\n}\n\n// OXIDIAN END\n\n// OXIDIAN BEGIN — frontmatter and title helpers\n\n/// Extracts the first `# Heading` as the note title, or the first non-empty line.\nfn extract_title(content: &str) -> Option<String> {\n    for line in content.lines() {\n        let trimmed = line.trim();\n        if let Some(stripped) = trimmed.strip_prefix(\"# \") {\n            return Some(stripped.trim().to_owned());\n        }\n        // Skip frontmatter delimiters and empty lines\n        if !trimmed.is_empty() && trimmed != \"---\" && trimmed != \"+++\" {\n            return Some(trimmed.to_owned());\n        }\n    }\n    None\n}\n\n/// Extracts tags from YAML frontmatter `tags:` field.\n/// Supports both `tags: [a, b]` and `tags:\\n  - a\\n  - b` formats.\nfn extract_tags_from_frontmatter(content: &str) -> Vec<String> {\n    let mut tags = Vec::new();\n    let mut in_frontmatter = false;\n    let mut in_tags_block = false;\n    let mut first_line = true;\n\n    for line in content.lines() {\n        let trimmed = line.trim();\n\n        if first_line && trimmed == \"---\" {\n            in_frontmatter = true;\n            first_line = false;\n            continue;\n        }\n        first_line = false;\n\n        if !in_frontmatter {\n            break;\n        }\n\n        if trimmed == \"---\" || trimmed == \"+++\" {\n            break;\n        }\n\n        if let Some(rest) = trimmed.strip_prefix(\"tags:\") {\n            let value = rest.trim();\n            if value.starts_with('[') && value.ends_with(']') {\n                // Inline array: tags: [rust, zed]\n                let inner = &value[1..value.len() - 1];\n                for tag in inner.split(',') {\n                    let tag = tag.trim().trim_matches('\"').trim_matches('\\'');\n                    if !tag.is_empty() {\n                        tags.push(tag.to_owned());\n                    }\n                }\n                in_tags_block = false;\n            } else if value.is_empty() {\n                // Block array follows\n                in_tags_block = true;\n            }\n            continue;\n        }\n\n        if in_tags_block {\n            if let Some(tag) = trimmed.strip_prefix(\"- \") {\n                let tag = tag.trim().trim_matches('\"').trim_matches('\\'');\n                if !tag.is_empty() {\n                    tags.push(tag.to_owned());\n                }\n            } else if !trimmed.is_empty() `.oxidian` marker (our vault),\n/// or an `.obsidian` directory (an Obsidian vault we can read).\npub fn is_vault_root(path: &Path) -> bool {\n    path.join(\".oxidian\").exists() || path.join(\".obsidian\").exists()\n}\n\n/// Builds a `VaultConfig` for the given root, importing Obsidian settings if present.\npub fn load_vault_config(root: PathBuf) -> VaultConfig {\n    let std::fs::read_to_string(&obsidian_config) {\n            import_obsidian_config(&mut config, &content);\n        }\n    }\n\n    config\n}\n\n/// Reads relevant fields from Obsidian's `app.json` and applies them to the config.\nfn import_obsidian_config(config: &mut VaultConfig, app_json: &str) {\n    let Ok(value) = serde_json::from_str::<serde_json::Value>(app_json) else {\n        return;\n    };\n\n    if let Some(attachment_folder) = value\n        .get(\"attachmentFolderPath\")\n        .and_then(|v| v.as_str())\n    {\n        config.templates_dir = config.root.join(attachment_folder);\n    }\n\n    if let Some(new_folder) = value\n        .get(\"newFileFolderPath\")\n        .and_then(|v| v.as_str())\n    {\n        // newFileFolderPath is where new notes go — we map this to the vault root behavior\n        let _ = new_folder; // stored for future use\n    }\n}\n\n// OXIDIAN END\n\n// OXIDIAN BEGIN — GPUI global registration\n\n/// GPUI global holding the active vault index, if any.\npub struct ActiveVault(pub Option<Entity<VaultIndex>>);\n\nimpl Global for ActiveVault {}\n\n/// Registers Oxidian vault integration with the GPUI App.\n/// Call this from `zed/src/main.rs` during initialization.\npub fn init(fs: Arc<dyn Fs>, cx: &mut App) {\n    cx.set_global(ActiveVault(None));\n    cx.set_global(oxidian_core::MarksmanBinaryPath(None));\n\n    cx.set_global(WikiLinkResolver(Arc::new(move |target, _window, cx| {\n        let active_vault = cx.try_global::<ActiveVault>().and_then(|av| av.0.clone())?;\n        let note_id = active_vault.read(cx).resolve_wiki_link(target);\n        if let Some(note_id) = note_id {\n            active_vault.read(cx).resolve_note(&note_id).cloned()\n        } else {\n            // Note does not exist yet! Create it under the vault root\n            let vault_root = active_vault.read(cx).config.root.clone();\n            let note_path = vault_root.join(format!(\"{}.md\", target));\n            if !note_path.exists() {\n                if let Some(parent) = note_path.parent() {\n                    let _ = std::fs::create_dir_all(parent);\n                }\n                let _ = std::fs::write(&note_path, format!(\"# {}\\n\\n\", target));\n            }\n            Some(note_path)\n        }\n    })));\n\n    cx.observe_new(move |workspace: &mut workspace::Workspace, })\n    .detach();\n}\n\n// OXIDIAN END\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_extract_wiki_links_simple() {\n        let text = \"See [[My Note]] for App.\n/// Call this from `zed/src/main.rs` during initialization.\npub fn init(fs: Arc<dyn Fs>, cx: &mut App) {\n    cx.set_global(ActiveVault(None));\n    cx.set_global(oxidian_core::MarksmanBinaryPath(None));\n\n    cx.set_global(WikiLinkResolver(Arc::new(move |target, _window, cx| {\n        let active_vault = cx.try_global::<ActiveVault>().and_then(|av| av.0.clone())?;\n        let note_id = active_vault.read(cx).resolve_wiki_link(target);\n        if let Some(note_id) = note_id {\n            active_vault.read(cx).resolve_note(&note_id).cloned()\n        } else {\n            // Note does not exist yet! std::fs::write(&note_path, format!(\"# {}\\n\\n\", target));\n            }\n            Some(note_path)\n        }\n    })));\n\n    cx.observe_new(move |workspace: &mut workspace::Workspace, _window, cx| {\n        let Some(worktree) = workspace.visible_worktrees(cx).next() else {\n            return;\n        };\n        let root_path = worktree.read(cx).abs_path().to_path_buf();\n\n index = cx.new(|cx| VaultIndex::new(config, fs.clone(), cx));\n            cx.update_global::<ActiveVault, _>(|active, _| {\n                active.0 = Some(index);\n            });\n        }\n    })\n    .detach();\n}\n\n// OXIDIAN END\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_extract_wiki_links_simple() {\n        let text = \"See [[My Note]] for details.\\nAlso [[Another Note|Display]] here.\";\n        let links = extract_wiki_links_from_text(text);\n        assert_eq!(links.len(), 2);\n        assert_eq!(links[0].0, 1);\n OpenTodayNote]);\n\npub fn init(cx: &mut App) {\n    cx.observe_new(|workspace: &mut Workspace, _, _| {\n        workspace.register_action(|workspace, _action: &ToggleDailyNotesPanel, window, cx| {\n            workspace.toggle_panel_focus::<DailyNotesPanel>(window, cx);\n        });\n\n        workspace.register_action(|workspace, _action: &OpenTodayNote, window, cx| {\n            let today = Local::now().naive_local().date();\n            open_daily_note_for_date(today, workspace.weak_handle(), window, cx);\n        });\n    })\n    .detach();\n}\n\nfn convert_obsidian_format_to_chrono(obsidian_format: &str) -> String {\n    obsidian_format\n        .replace(\"YYYY\", \"%Y\")\n        .replace(\"YY\", \"%y\")\n        .replace(\"MM\", \"%m\")\n        .replace(\"DD\", \"%d\")\n}\n\npub fn open_daily_note_for_date(\n    date: NaiveDate,\n    workspace: WeakEntity<Workspace>,\n    window: &mut Window,\n    cx: &mut App,\n) {\n    let Some(active_vault) = cx.try_global::<ActiveVault>().and_then(|av| av.0.clone()) else {\n        return;\n    };\n\n    let vault = active_vault.read(cx);\n    let daily_dir = vault.config.daily_notes_dir.clone();\n    let format_str = vault.config.daily_notes_format.clone();\n    let templates_dir = vault.config.templates_dir.clone();\n\n    let chrono_format = convert_obsidian_format_to_chrono(&format_str);\n    let date_str = date.format(&chrono_format).to_string();\n    let entry_path = daily_dir.join(format!(\"{}.md\", date_str));\n\n    let template_path = templates_dir.join(\"daily.md\");\n\n    let entry_path_clone = entry_path.clone();\n    let date_clone = date;\n    let format_str_clone = format_str.clone();\n\n    let create_task = cx.background_spawn(async move {\n        if !entry_path_clone.exists() {\n            if let Some(parent) = entry_path_clone.parent() {\n                std::fs::create_dir_all(parent)?;\n            }\n\n            let mut content = String::new();\n            if template_path.exists() {\n                if let Ok(tpl) = std::fs::read_to_string(&template_path) {\n                    content = tpl;\n                }\n            }\n\n            if content.is_empty() {\n                content = format!(\"# {}\\n\\n\", date_str);\n            } else {\n                let now_time = Local::now().format(\"%H:%M\").to_string();\n                let yesterday = date_clone.pred_opt().unwrap_or(date_clone);\n                let chrono_format = convert_obsidian_format_to_chrono(&format_str_clone);\n                let yesterday_str = yesterday.format(&chrono_format).to_string();\n\n                content = content\n                    .replace(\"{{date}}\", &date_str)\n                    .replace(\"{{time}}\", &now_time)\n                    .replace(\"{{yesterday}}\", &format!(\"[[{yesterday_str}]]\"));\n            }\n\n            std::fs::write(&entry_path_clone, content)?;\n        }\n        anyhow::Ok(entry_path_clone)\n    });\n\n    window\n        .spawn(cx, async move |cx| {\n            if let Ok(path) = create_task.await {\n                if let Some(workspace) = workspace.upgrade() {\n                    let _ = workspace.update_in(cx, |workspace, window, cx| {\n                        workspace.open_paths(\n                            vec![path],\n                            workspace::OpenOptions {\n                                visible: Some(workspace::OpenVisible::All),\n                                ..Default::default()\n                            },\n                            None,\n                            window,\n                            cx,\n                        )\n                        .detach();\n                    });\n                }\n            }\n            anyhow::Ok(())\n        })\n        .detach();\n}\n\npub struct DailyNotesPanel {\n    workspace: WeakEntity<Workspace>,\n    focus_handle: FocusHandle,\n    current_month: u32,\n    current_year: i32,\n    selected_date: NaiveDate,\n    notes_with_daily_dates: HashSet<NaiveDate>,\n    position: DockPosition,\n    active: bool,\n    zoomed: bool,\n    flexible: bool,\n    default_size: Pixels,\n    _subscriptions: Vec<Subscription>,\n}\n\nimpl EventEmitter<PanelEvent> for DailyNotesPanel {}\n\nimpl DailyNotesPanel {\n    pub fn new(workspace: Entity<Workspace>, cx: &mut Context<Self>) -> Self {\n        let focus_handle = cx.focus_handle();\n        let today = Local::now().naive_local().date();\n        let mut this = Self {\n            workspace: workspace.downgrade(),\n            focus_handle,\n            current_month: today.month(),\n            current_year: today.year(),\n            selected_date: today,\n            notes_with_daily_dates: HashSet::new(),\n            position: DockPosition::Right,\n            active: false,\n            zoomed: false,\n            flexible: true,\n            default_size: Pixels::from(280.0),\n            _subscriptions: Vec::new(),\n        };\n\n        this._subscriptions.push(cx.subscribe(&workspace, move |this, _, event, cx| {\n            if let workspace::Event::ActiveItemChanged = event {\n                this.update_existing_notes(cx);\n            }\n        }));\n\n        // Defer initial update to avoid borrowing workspace while it is updating\n        let handle = cx.weak_entity();\n        cx.defer(move |cx| {\n            handle.update(cx, |this, cx| {\n                this.update_existing_notes(cx);\n            }).ok();\n        });\n\n        this\n    }\n\n    pub async fn load(\n        workspace: WeakEntity<Workspace>,\n        mut cx: AsyncWindowContext,\n    ) -> anyhow::Result<Entity<Self>> {\n        workspace.update_in(&mut cx, |_, _window, cx| {\n            let workspace_view = cx.entity();\n            cx.new(|cx| Self::new(workspace_view, cx))\n        })\n    }\n\n    fn update_existing_notes(&mut self, cx: &mut Context<Self>) {\n        let Some(active_vault) = cx.try_global::<ActiveVault>().and_then(|av| av.0.clone()) else {\n            return;\n        };\n\n        let vault = active_vault.read(cx);\n        let daily_dir = vault.config.daily_notes_dir.clone();\n        let format_str = vault.config.daily_notes_format.clone();\n\n        cx.spawn(async move |this, cx| {\n            let existing_dates = cx.background_spawn(async move {\n                let mut dates: HashSet<NaiveDate> = HashSet::new();\n                let chrono_format = convert_obsidian_format_to_chrono(&format_str);\n                if let Ok(entries) = std::fs::read_dir(daily_dir) {\n                    for entry in entries.flatten() {\n                        let path = entry.path();\n                        if path.extension().map_or(false, |ext| ext == \"md\") {\n                            if let Some(stem) = path.file_stem().and_then(|s| s.to_str()) {\n                                if let Ok(parsed_date) = NaiveDate::parse_from_str(stem, &chrono_format) {\n                                    dates.insert(parsed_date);\n                                }\n                            }\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n                dates\n            })\n            .await;\n\n            this.update(cx, |this, cx| {\n                this.notes_with_daily_dates = existing_dates;\n                cx.notify();\n            })\n            .ok();\n        })\n        .detach();\n    }\n\n    fn prev_month(&mut self, cx: &mut Context<Self>) {\n        if self.current_month == 1 {\n            self.current_month = 12;\n            self.current_year -= 1;\n        } else {\n            self.current_month -= 1;\n        }\n        self.update_existing_notes(cx);\n    }\n\n    fn next_month(&mut self, cx: &mut Context<Self>) {\n        if self.current_month == 12 {\n            self.current_month = 1;\n            self.current_year += 1;\n        } else {\n            self.current_month += 1;\n        }\n        self.update_existing_notes(cx);\n    }\n\n    fn select_day(&mut self, date: NaiveDate, window: &mut Window, cx: &mut Context<Self>) {\n        self.selected_date = date;\n        cx.notify();\n        open_daily_note_for_date(date, self.workspace.clone(), window, cx);\n    }\n}\n\nfn days_in_month(year: i32, month: u32) -> u32 {\n    match month {\n        1 | 3 | 5 | 7 | 8 | 10 | 12 => 31,\n        4 | 6 | 9 | 11 => 30,\n        2 => {\n            if (year % 4 == 0 && year % 100 != 0) || year % 400 == 0 {\n                29\n            } else {\n                28\n            }\n        }\n        _ => 30,\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Render for DailyNotesPanel {\n    fn render(&mut self, _window: &mut Window, cx: &mut Context<Self>) -> impl IntoElement {\n        let month_name = match self.current_month {\n            1 => \"January\",\n            2 => \"February\",\n            3 => \"March\",\n            4 => \"April\",\n            5 => \"May\",\n            6 => \"June\",\n            7 => \"July\",\n            8 => \"August\",\n            9 => \"September\",\n            10 => \"October\",\n            11 => \"November\",\n            12 => \"December\",\n            _ => \"Unknown\",\n        };\n\n        let month_title = format!(\"{} {}\", month_name, self.current_year);\n\n        let calendar_header = div()\n            .flex()\n            .items_center()\n            .justify_between()\n            .px_3()\n            .py_2()\n            .border_b_1()\n            .border_color(cx.theme().colors().border)\n            .child(\n                div()\n                    .flex()\n                    .items_center()\n                    .gap_2()\n                    .child(Icon::new(IconName::Book).color(Color::Muted))\n                    .child(\n                        Label::new(\"Daily Notes\")\n                            .weight(FontWeight::BOLD)\n                            .color(Color::Default)\n                    )\n            );\n\n        let navigation_header = div()\n            .flex()\n            .items_center()\n            .justify_between()\n            .px_3()\n            .py_1p5()\n            .child(\n                Label::new(month_title)\n                    .weight(FontWeight::SEMIBOLD)\n                    .color(Color::Default)\n            )\n            .child(\n                div()\n                    .flex()\n                    .items_center()\n                    .gap_1()\n                    .child(\n                        IconButton::new(\"prev-month\", IconName::ChevronLeft)\n                            .on_click(cx.listener(|this, _, _, cx| {\n                                this.prev_month(cx);\n                            }))\n                    )\n                    .child(\n                        IconButton::new(\"next-month\", IconName::ChevronRight)\n                            .on_click(cx.listener(|this, _, _, cx| {\n                                this.next_month(cx);\n                            }))\n                    )\n            );\n\n        // Generate grid cells\n        let first_day = NaiveDate::from_ymd_opt(self.current_year, self.current_month, 1).unwrap();\n        let weekday_num = first_day.weekday().number_from_monday(); // 1..=7\n        let prev_month_days = weekday_num - 1;\n\n        let (prev_year, prev_month) = if self.current_month == 1 {\n            (self.current_year - 1, 12)\n        } else {\n            (self.current_year, self.current_month - 1)\n        };\n        let prev_month_len = days_in_month(prev_year, prev_month);\n\n        let mut cells = Vec::new();\n\n        for i in (0..prev_month_days).rev() {\n            let day = prev_month_len - i;\n            let date = NaiveDate::from_ymd_opt(prev_year, prev_month, day).unwrap();\n            cells.push((date, false));\n        }\n\n        let current_month_len = days_in_month(self.current_year, self.current_month);\n        for day in 1..=current_month_len {\n            let date = NaiveDate::from_ymd_opt(self.current_year, self.current_month, day).unwrap();\n            cells.push((date, true));\n        }\n\n        let remaining = 42 - cells.len();\n        let (next_year, next_month) = if self.current_month == 12 {\n            (self.current_year + 1, 1)\n        } else {\n            (self.current_year, self.current_month + 1)\n        };\n        for day in 1..=remaining {\n            let date = NaiveDate::from_ymd_opt(next_year, next_month, day as u32).unwrap();\n            cells.push((date, false));\n        }\n\n        let weekdays_header = div()\n            .grid_cols(7)\n            .gap_1()\n            .px_3()\n            .py_1()\n            .children([\"Mo\", \"Tu\", \"We\", \"Th\", \"Fr\", \"Sa\", \"Su\"].iter().map(|day| {\n                div()\n                    .flex()\n                    .justify_center()\n                    .child(\n                        Label::new(*day)\n                            .size(LabelSize::XSmall)\n                            .color(Color::Muted)\n                    )\n            }));\n\n        let today = Local::now().naive_local().date();\n\n        let cells_views = cells.into_iter().enumerate().map(|(idx, (date, is_current))| {\n            let has_note = self.notes_with_daily_dates.contains(&date);\n            let is_today = date == today;\n            let is_selected = date == self.selected_date;\n\n            div()\n                .id((\"day\", idx))\n                .flex()\n                .flex_col()\n                .items_center()\n                .justify_center()\n                .aspect_ratio(1.0)\n                .rounded_md()\n                .cursor_pointer()\n                .when(!is_current, |s| s.opacity(0.4))\n                .when(is_today, |s| s.border_1().border_color(cx.theme().colors().element_active))\n                .when(is_selected, |s| s.bg(cx.theme().colors().element_active))\n                .when(!is_selected && is_current, |s| s.hover(|style| style.bg(cx.theme().colors().element_hover)))\n                .on_click(cx.listener(move |this, _, window, cx| {\n                    this.select_day(date, window, cx);\n                }))\n                .child(\n                    Label::new(format!(\"{}\", date.day()))\n                        .size(LabelSize::Small)\n                        .weight(if has_note || is_selected { FontWeight::BOLD } else { FontWeight::NORMAL })\n                        .color(if is_selected { Color::Default } else if has_note { Color::Default } else { Color::Muted })\n                )\n                .when(has_note, |this| {\n                    this.child(\n                        div()\n                            .w(px(3.0))\n                            .h(px(3.0))\n                            .rounded_full()\n                            .bg(cx.theme().colors().element_active)\n                    )\n                })\n        });\n\n        let grid = div()\n            .id(\"calendar-grid\")\n            .grid_cols(7)\n            .gap_1()\n            .px_3()\n            .py_1()\n            .children(cells_views);\n\n        div()\n            .id(\"daily-notes-panel-root\")\n            .flex()\n            .flex_col()\n            .h_full()\n            .bg(cx.theme().colors().panel_background)\n            .track_focus(&self.focus_handle(cx))\n            .child(calendar_header)\n            .child(navigation_header)\n            .child(weekdays_header)\n            .child(grid)\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Panel for DailyNotesPanel {\n    fn persistent_name() -> &'static str {\n        \"DailyNotesPanel\"\n    }\n\n    fn panel_key() -> &'static str {\n        \"DailyNotesPanel\"\n    }\n\n    fn position(&self, _window: &Window, _cx: &App) -> DockPosition {\n        self.position\n    }\n\n    fn position_is_valid(&self, _position: active_item.downcast::<editor::Editor>() {\n            self.active_editor = Some(editor.downgrade());\n            let multi_buffer = editor.read(cx).buffer().read(cx);\n            if let fn non_empty_arc(value: &str) -> Option<Arc<str>> {

    let chars: Vec<char> = line.chars().collect();
    if chars.len() < 4 {
        return None;
    }

    // Look backwards from col for "[["
    let mut open_idx = None;
    let cursor = col.min(chars.len().saturating_sub(1));
    for i in (0..=cursor.min(chars.len().saturating_sub(2))).rev() {
        if chars[i] == '[' && chars[i + 1] == '[' {
            open_idx = Some(i + 2);
            break;

        }

Diff: /home/julesklord/Proyectos/repos/oxidian/crates/oxidian_vault/src/oxidian_vault.rs
```

// OXIDIAN BEGIN — note path helpers

fn note_path_for_target(vault_root: &Path, target: &str) -> Option<PathBuf> {
    let normalized = target.trim().trim_end_matches(".md").replace('\\', "/");
    let relative = Path::new(&normalized);

    if normalized.is_empty() || relative.is_absolute() {
        return None;
    }

    if relative.components().any(|component| {
        matches!(
            component,
            Component::ParentDir | Component::RootDir | Component::Prefix(_)
        )
    }) {
        return None;
    }

    Some(vault_root.join(relative).with_extension("md"))
}

// OXIDIAN END

// OXIDIAN BEGIN — GPUI global registration

```
